06/02/23, 6:00 pm - pritam: Good Evening Guys, 
As we all are aware that the whole state is currently disturbed because of a Supreme Court Verdict (dated: 13.01.2023) that clearly mentioned some unfavourable statements that has really hurt the sentiments of all the Nepali Community settled in Sikkim.
Therefore, supporting JAC (Joint Action Comittee) in 'Sikkim Bandh' on 8th of February , 2023 , Wednesday, we the students of SIST will be having a peaceful rally starting from our college till Jorethang. We, the SRC of SIST appeal each and everyone of you to join and support us to make it possible after all it's  overall an emotional moment for every Sikkimese. Everyone in support should be present in College dress ( the timing will be declared by tomorrow). We all know it's a matter of great concern for our as well as our upcoming generation identities. Let us all unite together and make this initiative a success.
Further, People willingly taking part in the rally, do make your friends and your group aware about the cause and the necessity of this initiative and encourage everyone to take part. Do join the following group mentioned below, if you will be joining us day after i.e 8th.
SRC Committee, SIST

07/03/23, 8:51 am - pritam: ⚠️ Important know hows for your DELD lab exam 

1. All of you are required to bring your lab files for final submission on the day of the exam. Submission of lab file is compulsory on the day of the exam

2. Out of all the experiments done , you will be asked to pick one experiment RANDOMLY. Once you have picked the experiment, no change of question is allowed. Make sure to study all the experiments properly

3. Apparatus required with proper specifications, quantity etc along with circuit diagrams needs to be shown to the examiner. IC PIN LAYOUT OF WHICHEVER IC YOU ARE USING IS COMPULSORY TO BE MADE , IRRESPECTIVE OF THE EXPERIMENT YOU ARE DOING. Once the examiner is satisfied, he will let you proceed with the conduction  of your experiment. 

4. Successfull conduction and record of the observations once done needs to be again shown to the examiner. 

5. Viva has a good weightage of marks, so make sure to study in details.

02/07/23, 1:35 pm - pritam: //This code belongs to Mr. Pritam and is designed to perform roundrobin algo with diffrent arrival time

#include <bits/stdc++.h>
using namespace std;
int main()
{
    queue<int> q;
    vector<int> at;
    vector<int> bt;
    vector<int> rbt;
    vector<int> tat;
    vector<int> wt;

    int *ct;
    //  vector<string> pid;

    int tq;
    int n, a;
    int value = 0;
    int count = 0;
    cout << "Enter the No of Process" << endl;
    cin >> n;
    ct = new int[n];
    cout << "Enter the time quantum" << endl;
    cin >> tq;
    cout << "Enter Process details" << endl;
    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
    {
        cout << "For Process:" << i + 1 << endl;

        //   string s;
        //   cin>>s;
        //   pid.push_back(s);
        cout << "Arrival time:";
        cin >> a;
        at.push_back(a);
        cout << "Burst Time:";
        cin >> a;
        bt.push_back(a);
        rbt.push_back(bt[i]);
    }
    cout << "Your entered details are" << endl;
    cout << "Arrival time           Burst Time" << endl;
    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
    {
        cout << "  " << at[i] << "                      " << bt[i] << endl;
    }

    for (int i = 0; i < n - 1; i++)
    {
        for (int j = i + 1; j < n; j++)
        {
            if (at[j] <= at[i])
            {
                swap(at[j], at[i]);
                swap(bt[j], bt[i]);
                swap(rbt[j], rbt[i]);
                // swap(pid[j],pid[i]);
            }
        }
    }
    cout << "Arrival time           Burst Time" << endl;
    for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
    {
        cout << "  " << at[i] << "                      " << bt[i] << "  " << rbt[i] << endl;
    }
    int temp = 0 - tq;
    int timer = 0;
    int val;

    q.push(at[0]);

    while (!q.empty())
    {

        temp = timer;

        if (rbt[q.front()] < tq)
        {
            timer = timer + rbt[q.front()];
            rbt[q.front()] = 0;
            // ct[q.front()]=timer;
            ct[q.front()] = timer;

            count++;
        }
        else
        {
            timer = tq + timer;
            rbt[q.front()] = rbt[q.front()] - tq;
            if (rbt[q.front()] == 0)
            {
                // ct[q.front()]=timer;
                ct[q.front()] = timer;
                count++;
            }
        }
        val = q.front();
        q.pop();

        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++)
        {
            if (at[i] > temp && at[i] <= timer)
            {
                q.push(i);
            }
        }

        if (rbt[val] != 0)
        {
            q.push(val);
        }
    }
    for(int i=0;i<n;i++){
        a=ct[i]-at[i];
        tat.push_back(a);
        a=tat[i]-bt[i];
        wt.push_back(a);
    }
    cout<<"At   Bt    Ct    TAT   Wt"<<endl;
    for(int i=0;i<n;i++){
        cout<<at[i]<<"       "<<bt[i]<<"      "<<ct[i]<<"      "<<tat[i]<<"      "<<wt[i]<<endl;
    }
    int sum=0;
    for(int i=0;i<n;i++){
        sum=sum+tat[i];
    }
    cout<<endl<<"Average TAT is: "<<float(sum)/float(n)<<endl;
    sum=0;
    for(int i=0;i<n;i++){
        sum=sum+wt[i];
    }
    cout<<endl<<"Average WT is: "<<float(sum)/float(n);

    
}

29/02/24, 1:36 pm - Bhupesh Da: Hello everyone,
Yesterday, Pragya Ma'am discussed the formation of groups for our mini projects. Each group should consist of four students, and we have the flexibility to choose our own groups initially. 18/03/24, 9:21 am - Mr. kerung: Instruction-level parallelism: ILP, or instruction-level parallelism, is a parallel computing concept that focuses on running several instructions concurrently on a single processor. Instead of relying on numerous processors or computing resources, it seeks to utilize the natural parallelism present in a program at the instruction level.

Instructions are carried out consecutively by traditional processors, one after the other. Nevertheless, many programs contain independent instructions that can be carried out concurrently without interfering with one another's output. To increase performance, instruction-level parallelism seeks to recognize and take advantage of these separate instructions.
